  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_2b9ff229-6d59-498b-b662-5429b24e349d'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<span id="freeTextContainer3911785738362232966"><b>An Amazon Charts and <i>Washington Post</i> bestseller.</b><br/><br/>Overworked and underappreciated, single mom Amy Byler needs a break. So when the guilt-ridden husband who abandoned her shows up and offers to take care of their kids for the summer, she accepts his offer and escapes rural Pennsylvania for New York City.<br/><br/>Usually grounded and mild mannered, Amy finally lets her hair down in the</span>
  <span id="freeText3911785738362232966" style="display:none"><b>An Amazon Charts and <i>Washington Post</i> bestseller.</b><br /><br />Overworked and underappreciated, single mom Amy Byler needs a break. So when the guilt-ridden husband who abandoned her shows up and offers to take care of their kids for the summer, she accepts his offer and escapes rural Pennsylvania for New York City.<br /><br />Usually grounded and mild mannered, Amy finally lets her hair down in the city that never sleeps. She discovers a life filled with culture, sophistication, and—with a little encouragement from her friends—a few blind dates. When one man in particular makes quick work of Amy’s heart, she risks losing herself completely in the unexpected escape, and as the summer comes to an end, Amy realizes too late that she must make an impossible decision: stay in this exciting new chapter of her life, or return to the life she left behind.<br /><br />But before she can choose, a crisis forces the two worlds together, and Amy must stare down a future where she could lose both sides of herself, and every dream she’s ever nurtured, in the beat of a heart.</span>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">It depends on your definition. No gutter mouth profanity, no offensive sex profanity. A smatter of descriptive and appropriate profanity of the every <a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">It depends on your definition. No gutter mouth profanity, no offensive sex profanity. A smatter of descriptive and appropriate profanity of the every day variety. In my definition, this book would be appropriate for a mom AND her teen daughter to share because it explores the issues of self worth, happiness, coming-of-age, and family relationships with honesty and humor.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>

<div id="review_2815004840" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2815004840" />
    <a title="Meredith" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30978160-meredith"><img alt="Meredith" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1423329725p2/30978160.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2815004840?book_show_action=true">May 12, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Meredith" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Meredith" href="/user/show/30978160-meredith">Meredith</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30978160-meredith?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2815004840" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14891712426542866963"><b>
  <i>Smart, savvy writing turns a predictable plot into a humorous and heartwarming read about a single mother’s journey to self-awareness.</i>
</b><br/><br/>Amy Byler is a single mom who does what it takes to provide for her children--in doing so, she has lost herself as she only sees herself as a mother to Cori and Joe. Three years ago, her husband walked out on her and their two teenage children. When he suddenly returns, he attempts to make amends by having their kids stay with him for a week over the summer. W</span>
  <span id="freeText14891712426542866963" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>Smart, savvy writing turns a predictable plot into a humorous and heartwarming read about a single mother’s journey to self-awareness.</i>
</b><br /><br />Amy Byler is a single mom who does what it takes to provide for her children--in doing so, she has lost herself as she only sees herself as a mother to Cori and Joe. Three years ago, her husband walked out on her and their two teenage children. When he suddenly returns, he attempts to make amends by having their kids stay with him for a week over the summer. WIth no one to take care of, Amy finds herself attending a librarian conference in NYC. While in the city, she reunites with an old friend who convinces her to take a momspringa (a play on the Amish Rumspringa). Away from her children and ex-husband, Amy slowly learns to come to terms with her failed marriage and being a mother. At the same time, she opens her mind to a new kind of life and new love. <br /><br />Amy’s character is likable and relatable, but her quick wit is what I loved best about her--she has a way with words. <b>
  <i> Kelly Harms’ witty writing style makes The Overdue Life of Amy Byler a standout. Amy’s snappy banter coupled with witty side characters gives this book a Gilmoreesque quality. In addition, there are tons of literary references that will be sure to make any book nerd smile with glee! </i>
</b>This is a light and charming read elevated by Harms' sharp, witty writing! #momspringa!<br /><br />I received an ARC of this book from NetGalley and Lake Union Publishing in exchange for an honest review.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14891712426542866963" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14231703937129434890">2.5 stars, rounded up<br/><br/>When will I ever learn? I keep thinking I’ll enjoy a romantic comedy. I WANT to like romantic comedies. But in truth, I tend to find most of them too simplistic for my taste. They usually start ok and then get dorky. This one tried to be more than just a rom-com with some single parent angst and a family crisis towards the end. But it just didn’t work for me. A little too simplistic and saccharine sweet. <br/><br/> The book is told from two viewpoints, Amy’s narrative and her daughter</span>
  <span id="freeText14231703937129434890" style="display:none">2.5 stars, rounded up<br /><br />When will I ever learn? I keep thinking I’ll enjoy a romantic comedy. I WANT to like romantic comedies. But in truth, I tend to find most of them too simplistic for my taste. They usually start ok and then get dorky. This one tried to be more than just a rom-com with some single parent angst and a family crisis towards the end. But it just didn’t work for me. A little too simplistic and saccharine sweet. <br /><br /> The book is told from two viewpoints, Amy’s narrative and her daughter’s journal entries. Amy, a single parent, finally gets a week to herself when her missing husband returns home after three years away and offers to watch the teenage kids. I’m not sure who irritated me more, Amy or her daughter. Neither came across as real. <br /><br />I am clearly in the minority here. Lots of other readers have given this high ratings. So, consider this the raving of an old grump that can’t appreciate a rom-com. <br /><br />Kudos though to the narrator who did a good job differentiating the voices. <br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_2666033412" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2666033412" />
    <a title="Christine" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/26175098-christine"><img alt="Christine" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1453924875p2/26175098.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2666033412?book_show_action=true">Feb 19, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christine" href="/user/show/26175098-christine">Christine</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/42399951-the-overdue-life-of-amy-byler">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26175098-christine?shelf=contemporary-fiction">contemporary-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26175098-christine?shelf=net-galley">net-galley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26175098-christine?shelf=ebooks">ebooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26175098-christine?shelf=womens-fiction">womens-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/26175098-christine?shelf=asked-to-review">asked-to-review</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2666033412" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11450167345591570284">I have been reading some heavy novels recently and thought it was time for something a little less oppressive. This one fit the bill perfectly.<br/><br/>Amy Byler is a school librarian and single mom with two kids, ages 12 and 15. Her husband up and left them for nebulous reasons three years previously. It has been a struggle to make things work, but Amy has indeed made a good life for her family even though she is worn down from her efforts. Suddenly Amy’s husband reappears and wants three months of re-b</span>
  <span id="freeText11450167345591570284" style="display:none">I have been reading some heavy novels recently and thought it was time for something a little less oppressive. This one fit the bill perfectly.<br /><br />Amy Byler is a school librarian and single mom with two kids, ages 12 and 15. Her husband up and left them for nebulous reasons three years previously. It has been a struggle to make things work, but Amy has indeed made a good life for her family even though she is worn down from her efforts. Suddenly Amy’s husband reappears and wants three months of re-bonding time with the kids, which eventually results in Amy getting a “momspringa” vacation in New York City.<br /><br />This book is engaging, funny, and thought provoking. Amy finally has time to actually think about finding her true self, and to try to determine in what direction she wants her life to go. Things are complex, and Amy has much to sort through. What exactly does her husband want? How will the kids react to him? Does she still love him or is she ready to move on to someone else? Her whole recent adult life has revolved around being a wonderful mother to her kids. But at what cost to herself? Is it possible to find a way to take better care of Amy? The cast includes a couple of great longtime friends of Amy’s - a magazine editor and an ex-nun (whom I loved) who dole out advice and a couple of interesting male companions Amy connects with during her journey in New York. <br /><br />Amy has a ton of decision trees in this novel, and it was fun to think about what I would do in her position. Humor is present throughout; I smiled a lot and laughed out loud several times. I also liked the fact that two of the main characters are librarians and we get some good librarian book talk in this story. Extra credit goes to Ms. Harms for her dialogue, which simply sparkles. <br /><br />Amy is so easy to cheer for and I kept hoping for a way for everything to fall into place for her and her family. I looked forward to grabbing the book every time I had a few minutes to read; I felt invested in the characters and was engrossed in their story.<br /><br />I recommend The Overdue Life of Amy Byler to anyone looking for a quick, easy, and fun read featuring a very likeable main character on a thoughtful journey. <br /><br />Thank you Net Galley, Lake Union Publishing, and Kelly Harms for the gift of an advanced review copy. Thanks also to Sonja Yoerg for kindly bringing this book to my attention. Opinions are mine alone and are not biased in any way. <br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11450167345591570284" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2786334743" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2786334743" />
    <a title="Larry H" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5872506-larry-h"><img alt="Larry H" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577826084p2/5872506.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2786334743?book_show_action=true">Apr 14, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Larry H" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Larry H" href="/user/show/5872506-larry-h">Larry H</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/42399951-the-overdue-life-of-amy-byler">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5872506-larry-h?shelf=kindle-first">kindle-first</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2786334743" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1833731744451290163">I'm between 3.5 and 4 stars, so I'll round up.<br/><br/>"I have suffered plenty. I am a poster child for low-grade chronic suffering. If an ad agency wanted to make suffering into a thirty-second spot, they would make a time-lapse video of me in my three colors of elastic-waistband teacher pants shoveling eight inches of snow at five a.m. so my kids can get to their early-bird activities on time, then teaching 250 overprivileged kids how to not use computers for porn for ten hours, and then collapsing in </span>
  <span id="freeText1833731744451290163" style="display:none">I'm between 3.5 and 4 stars, so I'll round up.<br /><br />"I have suffered plenty. I am a poster child for low-grade chronic suffering. If an ad agency wanted to make suffering into a thirty-second spot, they would make a time-lapse video of me in my three colors of elastic-waistband teacher pants shoveling eight inches of snow at five a.m. so my kids can get to their early-bird activities on time, then teaching 250 overprivileged kids how to not use computers for porn for ten hours, and then collapsing in front of <i>
  <b>Outlander</b>
</i> too tired to even find, much less turn on, my vibrator at the end of the day."<br /><br />For the last three years, Amy Byler has been the sole provider for her two children: 15-year-old Cori and 12-year-old Joe. She's barely keeping her head above water financially, working as a school librarian in order to keep her kids in private school, tending to the myriad repair needs of their beautiful yet historic (read: old) Pennsylvania house, and doing all of the disciplining, the chauffeuring, and everything else. That's been the drill since her husband left for a business trip in Hong Kong and decided not to come back.<br /><br />But now, John <i>is</i> back. He's realized he has been a terrible father and he wants to be a part of his children's lives again. He asks Amy to give him a week with the kids so he can begin seeking their forgiveness. (Much to Amy's chagrin, he accepts all of her criticisms and angry insults, and keeps apologizing, but he doesn't seem too interested in <i>her</i> forgiveness.) Reluctantly, she takes him up on his offer, and heads to New York for a week to attend a library conference.<br /><br />When Amy arrives in New York, the scene of some crazy college days, she's looking forward to a week of professional development, sleeping in, and reading a ton of books. Instead, she starts to let her hair down a little bit, and even meets a handsome librarian along the way. But she still can't stop worrying about her husband spending time with the kids, whether he's going to make some colossal mistake, or—worse—whether her kids will even miss her.<br /><br />Her old college friend, now the editor of a lifestyle magazine, convinces/orders Amy to get a total makeover, and sets her on a course for a real vacation from parenting, a #momspringa, if you will. When her husband asks to spend the summer with the kids, Amy's newfound freedom turns into a real adventure followed by the magazine's readers. She takes advantage of all the city has to offer and starts finding herself again, even going on a few blind dates. But when one man threatens to steal her heart, she has to decide whether this "new Amy" will still exist when she returns home, and what it means for everything—and everyone—if she doesn't.<br /><br /><b>
  <i>The Overdue Life of Amy Byler</i>
</b> was utterly charming, laugh-out-loud funny in parts, and an enjoyably thought-provoking read. Not being a woman or a parent, I may have missed some of the nuances of the story, but I think the book did a great job exploring the challenges women face as mothers, when they sacrifice everything else for their children and supporting their family. But when they do that, do they put their relationship with their spouse at risk, too, or is that something they shouldn't worry about?<br /><br />I enjoyed many of the characters in this book, from Amy to her former-nun-now-teacher best friend Lena, "hot librarian" Daniel to self-absorbed magazine diva Talia. Sure, the plot is a bit predictable, and I felt like it dragged a bit in the middle, but I was looking for a lighter read and this book definitely delivered. This definitely fits the bill when you've been reading a lot of brooding thrillers or books heavy on emotion—while there is still poignancy here, Kelly Harms keeps the tone light as she explores serious issues.<br /><br />Are you in need of a #momspringa? Wish you could have had one? <b>
  <i>The Overdue Life of Amy Byler</i>
</b> will give you the lowdown, and entertain you, to boot.<br /><br />Lake Union Publishing and Amazon First Reads provided me an advance copy of this book in exchange for an unbiased review. Thanks for making it available!<br /><br />The book will be published May 1, 2019. <br /><br />See all of my reviews at <a href="http://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com</a>.<br /><br />Check out my list of the best books I read in 2018 at <a href="https://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com/2019/01/the-best-books-i-read-in-2018.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">https://itseithersadnessoreuphoria.blogspot.com/2019/01/the-best-books-i-read-in-2018.html</a>. <br /><br />You can follow me on Instagram at <a href="https://www.instagram.com/yrralh/" target="”_blank”" rel="nofollow noopener"> https://www.instagram.com/yrralh/.</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="1833731744451290163" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<tr class="no_border feedFooterReview" id="update_comment_stuff_Review2786334743">

<div id="review_2822963793" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2822963793" />
    <a title="Sherry Mabry" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13916432-sherry-mabry"><img alt="Sherry Mabry" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1351077331p2/13916432.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2822963793?book_show_action=true">May 21, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sherry Mabry" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sherry Mabry" href="/user/show/13916432-sherry-mabry">Sherry Mabry</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/42399951-the-overdue-life-of-amy-byler">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2822963793" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11675938452496538878">I have been slogging through a really difficult, and not particularly rewarding, book. So I thought this would be a light, amusing read - a nice break from the other book. Whew - I went from the arcane to the inane. She lost me at "Flexthology" - the main character's terribly named program to get kids to read, which we are supposed to believe just wowed a room full of educators and librarians (including, of course, the one-in-a-million hot librarian who presumably falls for her on the basis of f</span>
  <span id="freeText11675938452496538878" style="display:none">I have been slogging through a really difficult, and not particularly rewarding, book. So I thought this would be a light, amusing read - a nice break from the other book. Whew - I went from the arcane to the inane. She lost me at "Flexthology" - the main character's terribly named program to get kids to read, which we are supposed to believe just wowed a room full of educators and librarians (including, of course, the one-in-a-million hot librarian who presumably falls for her on the basis of flexthology). To sum up the program...give kids a choice of what to read. Well...duh. <br /><br />If flexthology wasn't bad enough...I cringed every time I read "momspringa"...literally cringed. Yes, yes...I've been a busy mom myself. We all need a break. But we don't get a magical Cinderella fairy tale of going away for the summer and by chance getting all our expenses paid. The plot was ridiculous. Here was my biggest issue...her "ex" seems to have some money. He abandoned her and her kids for 3 years! Despite the horrific psychologic damage you could reasonably assume would happen to all of them, there was also significant financial damage. ...except he didn't seem to totally abandon them. You come to realize there was SOME contact. And during that contact Amy didn't think to say, "HEY LOSER...I'M STRUGGLING TO MAKE ENDS MEET HERE - SEND SOME CHILD SUPPORT!" Come on. She didn't even ASK for him to live up to his responsibilities. And yet, when he shows up, he seems to be bending over backward to hand out money? <br /><br />And lucky Amy, not only does she go to NYC for the summer, she accidentally ends up with an apartment, an all expenses paid makeover, food tabs picked up, etc., etc., AND a hot librarian, who is kind, understanding, funny, great in bed and generally all around perfect. Except, alas, he shares custody of his teenage daughter and Amy has two teenagers in PA, and how EVER could they make that work. Really? Really? These are two college-educated grown ass adults madly in love and the only options they can come up with are just be friends or break up at the end of the summer? Because ya know...NY to PA...just insurmountable. <br /><br />It just didn't make sense and was all so, so unrealistic. It's enough to send me back to my serious, but boring book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11675938452496538878" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText4618648888415808297" style="display:none">this is your classic chick-lit: unexpected situation arises, women deals with unexpected situation, learns about herself in the process (while having men throw themselves at her), happy ending. <br /><br />im generally a sucker for these kind of stories, but something was missing for me to really relate to it. i want to say its because im just not at the point of life where ive been married, have an ex-husband, and children. but ive related to characters in this situation before, so im not sure why i just couldnt quite click with amy. <br /><br />overall, this is a cute story, but not one that stands out for me, personally. <br /><br /><b>↠ <i>2.5 stars</i></b></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=2019-publications">2019-publications</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=family">family</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=adult">adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3002300701" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9900563340373762224">Amy’s husband John abandoned her three years ago and though it was hard on her, she found a way to make life as a single mother work. But now John is back and wants to spend time with the kids. Reluctantly, Amy agrees and decides to go to New York where she ends up having a blast. #momspringa is on. <br/><br/>Though I don’t have children and am probably half of Amy Byler’s age, I was pretty entertained by this story and appreciated seeing a dedicated mom take care of her own self for once. Everything is r</span>
  <span id="freeText9900563340373762224" style="display:none">Amy’s husband John abandoned her three years ago and though it was hard on her, she found a way to make life as a single mother work. But now John is back and wants to spend time with the kids. Reluctantly, Amy agrees and decides to go to New York where she ends up having a blast. #momspringa is on. <br /><br />Though I don’t have children and am probably half of Amy Byler’s age, I was pretty entertained by this story and appreciated seeing a dedicated mom take care of her own self for once. Everything is realistic but with a touch of fantasy that reminds you that beautiful and exciting things can happen in life if you are open to them. <br /><br />Another thing I liked was how the author gave us both worlds: that of the attached mother who needs to be in contact with her children every day and that of the carefree mother who is set on having a good time free of motherly duties. While in New York, Amy goes on dates, spends time with an old friend, gets a makeover and even… has sex. Gasp! A one-night stand or the start of something new?<br /><br />But she does think of her daughter Cori and son Joe constantly. Every chapter basically begins with a message from Cori telling her what she is up to and especially what books she is currently reading seeing that Amy, a school librarian, encourages reading in her family. I found those letters/emails very touching and I was always happy to read them. <br /><br />Recommended to those who enjoy contemporary romances and family-themed stories. <br /><br /><a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a>Twitter</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/hit-miss-books-12564715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a><br /></span>

<div id="review_2771437720" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2771437720" />
    <a title="Bridgett" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2048557-bridgett"><img alt="Bridgett" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1549460817p2/2048557.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2771437720?book_show_action=true">Apr 07, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bridgett" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bridgett" href="/user/show/2048557-bridgett">Bridgett</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2048557-bridgett?shelf=arc">arc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2771437720" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4006699357270708714"><i>
  <b>I'm in the minority on this one.</b>
</i><br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/41723475.The_Overdue_Life_of_Amy_Byler' title='The Overdue Life of Amy Byler by Kelly Harms' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Overdue Life of Amy Byler</a> is a cute, quick, <u>predictable</u> read. What you expect to happen is exactly what happens. It's a character driven novel, which is fine...I don't need constant action when books are well-written. Unfortunately, the characters seemed very much like characters, and not actual people. The dialogue reminded me of an 80s sitcom where everyone spews one-liners...even the 12 year old. The voices of Amy (the mother) and Cori (her 15 year old </span>
  <span id="freeText4006699357270708714" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>I'm in the minority on this one.</b>
</i><br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/41723475.The_Overdue_Life_of_Amy_Byler" title="The Overdue Life of Amy Byler by Kelly Harms" rel="nofollow noopener">The Overdue Life of Amy Byler</a> is a cute, quick, <u>predictable</u> read. What you expect to happen is exactly what happens. It's a character driven novel, which is fine...I don't need constant action when books are well-written. Unfortunately, the characters seemed very much like characters, and not actual people. The dialogue reminded me of an 80s sitcom where everyone spews one-liners...even the 12 year old. The voices of Amy (the mother) and Cori (her 15 year old daughter) were virtually indistinguishable. And the constant corny jokes eventually became trite and tiresome. <br /><br />Neither negative, nor positive thoughts about this story abound...which sums the book up pretty well for me. It's an unmemorable, completely average novel. <br /><br /><b>2.5 stars</b><br /><br />**I received a free, advanced copy of this book through Amazon's Kindle First program. All opinions are my own.</span>

          </span>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jennifer ~ TarHeelReader" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jennifer ~ TarHeelReader" href="/user/show/32340179-jennifer-tarheelreader">Jennifer ~ TarHeelReader</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2815458700" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7198094819399348856">Amy Byler is a single mom with her hands full. When she’s feeling particularly overwrought, her estranged husband returns and offers to care for the kids for the summer. <br/><br/>Amy accepts, and she’s off to NYC. Amy has led a quiet life, but her alter ego comes out. She even goes on a couple blind dates. <br/><br/>One of the blind dates ends up capturing her heart, and when the summer is about to end, Amy has to decide between her new life and her old one. <br/><br/>Amy doesn’t get to make that choice, though, because bot</span>
  <span id="freeText7198094819399348856" style="display:none">Amy Byler is a single mom with her hands full. When she’s feeling particularly overwrought, her estranged husband returns and offers to care for the kids for the summer. <br /><br />Amy accepts, and she’s off to NYC. Amy has led a quiet life, but her alter ego comes out. She even goes on a couple blind dates. <br /><br />One of the blind dates ends up capturing her heart, and when the summer is about to end, Amy has to decide between her new life and her old one. <br /><br />Amy doesn’t get to make that choice, though, because both lives collide.<br /><br />Amy is the quintessential mom who has put her children and family ahead of herself for years. She’s made so many sacrifices she feels like she no longer knows herself. It was fun and entertaining to watch her make that discovery on her “momspringa.” <br /><br />The characters in the book are quite charming. Friends Talia, Daniel, and Lena really round out the story. Amy was always my favorite, though. She’s endearing and relatable, and I was captivated with how her life would turn out. I was fully absorbed in Amy’s story and loved all the bookish nods! This book is a true, refreshing escape! <br /><br />I received a complimentary copy. All opinions are my own.<br /><br />My reviews can also be found on my blog: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.jennifertarheelreader.com">www.jennifertarheelreader.com</a></span>

<div id="review_2742337693" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2742337693" />
    <a title="Berit☀️✨" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/38946743-berit"><img alt="Berit☀️✨" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1534383878p2/38946743.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2742337693?book_show_action=true">May 23, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Berit☀️✨" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Berit☀️✨" href="/user/show/38946743-berit">Berit☀️✨</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38946743-berit?shelf=arc-physical">arc-physical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38946743-berit?shelf=2019">2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38946743-berit?shelf=blog-tour">blog-tour</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2742337693" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16833760319065777922">🅡🅔🅛🅐🅣🅐🅑🅛🅔. 🅗🅘🅛🅐🅡🅘🅞🅤🅢. 🅕🅐🅝🅣🅐🅑🅤🅛🅞🅤🅢.<br/><br/> Kelly harms! BRAVO! This was such a relatable story told with so much heart and humor, I absolutely adored it! Amy is the single mother of 15-year-old Cory and 12-year-old Joe. Three years ago Amy’s husband John went out of country for work and never came back. Amy picked her self up, dusted herself off, went back to work, and learned how to be a single parent. Now John is back wanting to repair his relationship with his Children and offering Amy a summer off f</span>
  <span id="freeText16833760319065777922" style="display:none">🅡🅔🅛🅐🅣🅐🅑🅛🅔. 🅗🅘🅛🅐🅡🅘🅞🅤🅢. 🅕🅐🅝🅣🅐🅑🅤🅛🅞🅤🅢.<br /><br /> Kelly harms! BRAVO! This was such a relatable story told with so much heart and humor, I absolutely adored it! Amy is the single mother of 15-year-old Cory and 12-year-old Joe. Three years ago Amy’s husband John went out of country for work and never came back. Amy picked her self up, dusted herself off, went back to work, and learned how to be a single parent. Now John is back wanting to repair his relationship with his Children and offering Amy a summer off from parental responsibility. What follows is Amy’s summer of freedom, fun, self discovery, love, and a new wardrobe. #momspringa<br /><br /> Amy was such a real and relatable character. As a single mother I saw so much of myself in Amy. It is so easy to get caught up in your kids lives and not make enough time for yourself. But you also don’t know who you are if you’re not a mom. It was so much fun reading about Amy rediscovering herself in New York. I loved the makeover, all the shopping, and all the crazy dates. I also loved her support system her Besties Lena and Tallia, and Mathew who was kind of a bit of a fairy godfather. Also loved the big part that books played in this story. Amy was a librarian and she had this really interesting program she presented at a librarian convention. I’m sure all bookworms will appreciate the amount of booktalk in this book. And there is a hot librarian love interest. Another part of the book I really loved was Corey’s journal entries, Kelly harms really nailed the 15-year-old voice. There was just so much fun and goodness in this book!<br /><br /> This is one of those books that will make you smile, make you laugh, and leave you feeling good when you have turned that last page. The characters are relatable, likable, and entertaining. The storyline is amusing and authentic. I think all moms will absolutely love this book! BUT I think the book will not only appeal to Mom’s it will appeal to anyone who is ever needed a break from their real life, A little re-charge. Simply put this is an uplifting feel-good story with relatable characters and a lot of humor!<br /><br />*** Big thanks to Lake Union for my copy of this book ***</span>
  <a data-text-id="16833760319065777922" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_2802688432" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2802688432" />
    <a title="Brandice" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/36348070-brandice"><img alt="Brandice" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582594594p2/36348070.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2802688432?book_show_action=true">Jun 14, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brandice" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brandice" href="/user/show/36348070-brandice">Brandice</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/42399951-the-overdue-life-of-amy-byler">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2802688432" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3534283071034979220">This book was such a fun, heartwarming story! In <i>The Overdue Life of Amy Byler</i>, librarian Amy finds herself face-to-face with her separated husband John, who’s requesting permission to visit their children, Cori and Joe, after abandoning the family 3 years earlier. Amy is torn: dealing with her own unresolved feelings about John, and considering what’s truly best for their children. After discussions with the kids, Amy agrees to let John spend time with them in rural PA now that it’s summer. <br/><br/>Whi</span>
  <span id="freeText3534283071034979220" style="display:none">This book was such a fun, heartwarming story! In <i>The Overdue Life of Amy Byler</i>, librarian Amy finds herself face-to-face with her separated husband John, who’s requesting permission to visit their children, Cori and Joe, after abandoning the family 3 years earlier. Amy is torn: dealing with her own unresolved feelings about John, and considering what’s truly best for their children. After discussions with the kids, Amy agrees to let John spend time with them in rural PA now that it’s summer. <br /><br />While John catches up on dad duties, Amy goes to New York City to attend an educational conference and visit an old friend. She’s been out of the game, both socially and romantically, but attempts to come (back) into her own, slowly but surely. <br /><br />A few of my favorite quotes from the book:<br /><br />-<i>”He looks like that dad from a diversely cast CW show. In short: dreamy.”</i><br /><br />-<i>”Look at me throwing around my money like an oil heiress...”</i><br /><br />-<i>”I get this now. I get now that you can love what you have, love your kids and your life and your friends, and still want more. I get that it’s ok to go out out and get more, more love, more friendship, more fulfillment, and still be a wonderful mom.”</i><br /><br />Though I’m not a mom, there were a lot of relatable elements in Amy’s story and I liked her as a character. <i>The Overdue Life of Amy Byler</i> is cute and funny yet also fairly realistic. The truth is, we all just need a break sometimes! <br /><br /><i>Thank you to NetGalley and Lake Union Publishing for providing an advance copy in exchange for an honest review.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="3534283071034979220" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Jayme" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11345366-jayme"><img alt="Jayme" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1545654456p2/11345366.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2837319324?book_show_action=true">Feb 07, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jayme" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jayme" href="/user/show/11345366-jayme">Jayme</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/42399951-the-overdue-life-of-amy-byler">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11345366-jayme?shelf=women-s-fiction">women-s-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2837319324" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14644236548945321579">3.75 rounded up! <br/><br/>What does any “self-actualized, successful, capable adult woman” do when confronted in the drugstore by the husband who abandoned her and her two children? Try to duck behind the Q-tips, of course! <br/><br/>He has been gone for THREE years, but now John wants HIS life back. <br/><br/>When ducking behind the shelves fails, Amy reluctantly listens to what John has to say, and unselfishly agrees to allows him time with the kids, so he can attempt to mend his relationship with them. <br/><br/>With nothing to do</span>
  <span id="freeText14644236548945321579" style="display:none">3.75 rounded up! <br /><br />What does any “self-actualized, successful, capable adult woman” do when confronted in the drugstore by the husband who abandoned her and her two children? Try to duck behind the Q-tips, of course! <br /><br />He has been gone for THREE years, but now John wants HIS life back. <br /><br />When ducking behind the shelves fails, Amy reluctantly listens to what John has to say, and unselfishly agrees to allows him time with the kids, so he can attempt to mend his relationship with them. <br /><br />With nothing to do for the summer, Amy decides to attend a librarian’s conference in NY city where she can also reconnect with her college friend Talia, who works for a fashion magazine. <br /><br />Before she knows it, she has been given a makeover and a starring role in “#Momspringa, an article about a woman challenged to “rediscover” herself while on a mini vacation from single motherhood and its never ending responsibilities! <br /><br />A few blind dates, set up by the magazine, and a “friendship” with “hot librarian Daniel” make Amy feel as if she is on “The Bachelorette, Special Middle-Aged edition!” (Her words)<br /><br />But when summer ends, will Amy want HER life back? <br />Will it be enough?<br /><br />For me to enjoy Women’s fiction, I need a few things...<br />1. Witty dialogue that does not rely on sex and body part references to amuse. <br />2. Introspective passages from the protagonist which resonate with me and are highlight worthy.<br />3. A character I like and want to root for. <br /><br />This book checked those boxes. <br /><br />If you are not a book lover like myself, you may not completely understand a woman who who is looking forward to a week’s vacation so she can read the “six new books carefully chosen and downloaded to her Kindle!” <br /><br />But, I nodded my head and smiled when I read that! 📚😊<br /><br />Each chapter starts with an amusing journal entry from her “wise beyond her years” daughter, Cori...<br /><br />Also sprinkled throughout the book are sporadic text messages between Amy and her two closest friends, helping to move the book along despite the long chapters. <br /><br />Favorite quote from the book: “Love isn’t a feeling-it’s an action”.<br /><br />Thanks to my book buddy DeAnn, for reading this one with me! Always enjoy hearing your perspectives along the way!</span>
  <a data-text-id="14644236548945321579" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2808428103" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2808428103" />
    <a title="Carolyn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19559507-carolyn"><img alt="Carolyn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1546411572p2/19559507.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2808428103?book_show_action=true">May 09, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carolyn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carolyn" href="/user/show/19559507-carolyn">Carolyn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/42399951-the-overdue-life-of-amy-byler">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2808428103" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2431518665614882050">Kelly Harms has written a light, fun read about a middle aged librarian who gets a chance to have a summer to herself while her estranged husband re-bonds with his children.<br/><br/>When Amy Byler's husband went on a business trip to Hong Kong three years ago and never returned, she suddenly found herself a single, unemployed mother of two children with a large mortgage and no child support. Life gradually got better once she got herself a job as a school librarian and re-mortgaged the house, but she and</span>
  <span id="freeText2431518665614882050" style="display:none">Kelly Harms has written a light, fun read about a middle aged librarian who gets a chance to have a summer to herself while her estranged husband re-bonds with his children.<br /><br />When Amy Byler's husband went on a business trip to Hong Kong three years ago and never returned, she suddenly found herself a single, unemployed mother of two children with a large mortgage and no child support. Life gradually got better once she got herself a job as a school librarian and re-mortgaged the house, but she and the kids have had to budget carefully and she has got used to being a single parent, always on call as driver, carer and worrier.<br /><br />Out of the blue, her husband has returned with a wish to spend the summer reconnecting with the kids. Angry at first and then hesitant about handing over her kids, Amy goes to stay with her old college friend Talia in New York who is editor of a fashion and lifestyle magazine. She's looking forward to spending some time on her own sleeping in and reading books but Talia decides Amy needs a makeover, an agenda of activities and some hot dates. Talia calls it the 'momspringa' (like the Amish rumspringa) and decides to feature it in the magazine as something all mothers need now and again. Reluctant at first but with encouragement from Talia, her best friend ex-nun Lena and Daniel, the hot librarian she befriends at a librarians convention, Amy soon finds that she is enjoying her new improved self and breaking out of the stasis she has been in for the past three years.<br /><br />This was an engaging read with interesting characters who love talking about books and plays. Beware though, it may make you want to have a 'momspringa of your own!<br /><br /><i>With thanks to Netgalley and Lake Union Publishing for a digital ARC to read</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="2431518665614882050" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Kristy Harvey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/22318404-kristy-harvey"><img alt="Kristy Harvey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442985127p2/22318404.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2674151949" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17061921493844332860">Quit reading this review and go read this book! It is laugh-out-loud hilarious and I still can't figure out how Harms can so seamlessly transition from writing a snarky but charming teenager to writing a full grown woman in the midst of her #momspringa (Don't know what that is? Well, GO READ THE BOOK.) in a matter of a page. I could not put this book down!! I'd give it 10 stars if I could!</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2886584312" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2886584312" />
    <a title="Theresa Alan" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3268839-theresa-alan"><img alt="Theresa Alan" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1265739602p2/3268839.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2886584312?book_show_action=true">Jul 10, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Theresa Alan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Theresa Alan" href="/user/show/3268839-theresa-alan">Theresa Alan</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2886584312" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14764208571532674873">Amy was forced to be a single mother when her husband abandoned her and their two kids three years earlier. She cut back expenses, got a job as a school librarian, and survived without the help of any child support. When her husband abruptly shows up and wants to catch up with the kids over the summer, she agrees because she wants the children to have a good relationship with him even if she doesn’t.<br/><br/>Her old friend Talia lives in New York City and works at a fashion magazine, so Amy heads to New </span>
  <span id="freeText14764208571532674873" style="display:none">Amy was forced to be a single mother when her husband abandoned her and their two kids three years earlier. She cut back expenses, got a job as a school librarian, and survived without the help of any child support. When her husband abruptly shows up and wants to catch up with the kids over the summer, she agrees because she wants the children to have a good relationship with him even if she doesn’t.<br /><br />Her old friend Talia lives in New York City and works at a fashion magazine, so Amy heads to New York to attend a librarian conference and hang out with Talia. Talia’s assistant Matt basically forces Amy to undergo a makeover. What I really liked was that Amy never thought her life would magically get better with a cool haircut and fashionable clothes. She likes herself as the simple book-reading mom that she is. She does discover, however, that she likes really good bras that fit properly.<br /><br />A little romance plus agreeing to a little risk helps Amy grow emotionally over the summer to realize that time off from being a single mom who also works full time outside the home helps her be a better mother. <br /><br />This book is a lot of fun. <br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="14764208571532674873" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2824144983" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2824144983" />
    <a title="Melki" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5293536-melki"><img alt="Melki" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1308071306p2/5293536.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2824144983?book_show_action=true">May 17, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melki" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melki" href="/user/show/5293536-melki">Melki</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/42399951-the-overdue-life-of-amy-byler">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5293536-melki?shelf=humorous-fiction">humorous-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5293536-melki?shelf=family-based-fiction">family-based-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5293536-melki?shelf=librarians-gone-wild">librarians-gone-wild</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2824144983" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6870602444826365893"><b>Look at me. I am a modern woman! I am Gloria Steinem and Helen Gurley Brown and the slutty one from <i>Sex and the City</i> all wrapped up in one.</b><br/><br/>A straitlaced librarian mother of two gets to experience the glamorous life when her AWOL husband returns to entertain the kids for a few weeks. Her <b>momspringa</b> turns into a voyage of self discovery, makes her a minor celebrity, and instills a sassy new attitude in our plucky heroine. <br/><br/>There's no doubt that the film rights have already been sold, and with a few</span>
  <span id="freeText6870602444826365893" style="display:none"><b>Look at me. I am a modern woman! I am Gloria Steinem and Helen Gurley Brown and the slutty one from <i>Sex and the City</i> all wrapped up in one.</b><br /><br />A straitlaced librarian mother of two gets to experience the glamorous life when her AWOL husband returns to entertain the kids for a few weeks. Her <b>momspringa</b> turns into a voyage of self discovery, makes her a minor celebrity, and instills a sassy new attitude in our plucky heroine. <br /><br />There's no doubt that the film rights have already been sold, and with a few tweeks, this could be the next Melissa McCarthy vehicle.<br /><br />This is not the type of book I'd normally read, but I must admit I'm a sucker for tales of <b>librarians gone wild</b>. Though the writing is decent, and there's some great dialogue, it's really only a three-star read. However, I'm tacking on an extra twinkler as I think the author delivered exactly what was promised - an enjoyable, innocuous, rom-com romp.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6870602444826365893" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

One day the husband who abandoned her and her two children (Cori & Joe) returns and wants to bond with his kids. So he offers to take care of the children for the summer. <div id="review_2909989722" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2909989722" />
    <a title="Corina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8905971-corina"><img alt="Corina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1580618612p2/8905971.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2909989722?book_show_action=true">Jul 26, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Corina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Corina" href="/user/show/8905971-corina">Corina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/45421678-the-overdue-life-of-amy-byler">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8905971-corina?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8905971-corina?shelf=single-parent">single-parent</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2909989722" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6805976351194070550">I really enjoyed this audiobook.<br/><br/>It made me laugh and smile. Even though Amy was a bit over the top at times, emotionally all over the place, the plot, idea and execution was well done, and the story on its own was entertaining and the humor was right up my alley.<br/><br/>There were quite a few things I really enjoyed about this book.<br/><br/>Many of the chapters started with a journal entry from Amy’s teenage daughter. The author did a fabulous job portraying a teenage girl who is not a passionate reader, but who</span>
  <span id="freeText6805976351194070550" style="display:none">I really enjoyed this audiobook.<br /><br />It made me laugh and smile. Even though Amy was a bit over the top at times, emotionally all over the place, the plot, idea and execution was well done, and the story on its own was entertaining and the humor was right up my alley.<br /><br />There were quite a few things I really enjoyed about this book.<br /><br />Many of the chapters started with a journal entry from Amy’s teenage daughter. The author did a fabulous job portraying a teenage girl who is not a passionate reader, but whose mother is a librarian. It was quite the conundrum for both of them. And I loved how levelheaded her daughter was. She made me chuckle more than once with her wit and insightful remarks.<br /><br />I also loved Amy’s love interest, they clicked perfectly, and he was such an awesome guy – really amazing. I wouldn’t have said no to him – lol. Actually that’s one of the subplots I would have liked to have a bit more page time. They were such a cute couple and their common interest – books – was my favorite part of the story. Amy being a librarian played an interesting role in the overall plot line. It would have been great to dig a little bit deeper into that particular topic. Because it was quite a fascinating topic.<br /><br />Amy’s respite in New York was a wonderful change for her and a great interlude for me as a reader. Because if there is one thing I would change about this book, it was Amy’s seemingly never ending moaning about her estranged husband. They’ve been separated for years, and the time that the author dedicated to this particular subplot felt a bit excessive. .<br /><br />Nevertheless the book was a wonderfully poignant and touching story about motherhood, finding yourself again, being open to change, and accepting that being a mother doesn’t mean you can’t be still your own person.<br /><br />The letters at the end really brought the book to a very satisfying ending.<br /><br /><br />____________________________________<br /><br />___________________________________<br /><a href="https://thebrowneyedbookworm.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Find more reviews and book recommendations on my blog.</a><br /><br /><a href="https://www.instagram.com/thebrowneyedbookworm/" rel="nofollow noopener">Find me on Bookstagram.</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="6805976351194070550" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2823494304" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18380091683067762720"> In THE OVERDUE LIFE OF AMY BYLER by Kelly Harris, Amy has devoted all her life so far to the raising and care of her children. When they were nine and thirteen, her husband left, moving to Korea to get himself more emotionally stable and do what was right for him. Now, after three years he wants to come back and spend a week with the children he abandoned. He prefaces his proposal by apologizing for the hurt he’s caused and saying he wants to repair some of the damage.<br/>When Amy first hears the i</span>
  <span id="freeText18380091683067762720" style="display:none"> In THE OVERDUE LIFE OF AMY BYLER by Kelly Harris, Amy has devoted all her life so far to the raising and care of her children. When they were nine and thirteen, her husband left, moving to Korea to get himself more emotionally stable and do what was right for him. Now, after three years he wants to come back and spend a week with the children he abandoned. He prefaces his proposal by apologizing for the hurt he’s caused and saying he wants to repair some of the damage.<br />When Amy first hears the idea, she is absolutely against the plan. How can she trust him to take care of them after three years of being a single parent? How can she forgive him for the strife she has endured for these three years? What will she do if she take time for only herself? Yet, as her husband shows every possibility for actually being able to manage a week of single parenting she is encouraged by her friends to take the time for herself.<br />Once she agrees, Amy finds herself in New York, going to a librarian’s conference and rooming with an old friend from her single days, Talia. Talia encourages her to get rid of her mom jeans, put on some clothes from the designer closet belonging to the magazine where Talia works, and spread her wings a little while in the city.<br />Amy agrees and is suddenly swept up in a whirlwind with Talia’s assistant, that he has dubbed her “momspringa”. She gets a complete makeover, experiences some fancy New York restaurants, and is reminded of the person she was before she became “A MOM”. She has a great time at the conference, sharing a new reading plan with other librarians and making new friends including a “hot librarian.”<br />As the week comes to an end, her husband and children petition her to give them the entire summer. He has shown himself capable of parenting, plus has offered them camp experiences that are “once in a lifetime” opportunities; diving camp for their teenage daughter and space camp for their almost tween son. With no concrete evidence that this will do irreparable harm to either of the children coupled with the pull of a summer filled with experiences she has denied herself for the past few years, Amy agrees. She is still reluctant to think of it as a momspringa, but she is agreeable to having a few more exciting adventures before she returns home to begin full-time parenting again.<br />The book, the experiences, Amy reactions were all fully satisfying. This is a book every mother could benefit from reading, even if it doesn’t lead to a full-blown momspringa for them. Even for those moms who have no need to reconnect with another part of themselves, if those moms exist, there is plenty of entertainment and encouragement here. In short, it’s one of the best books I’ve ever read, even though I’m well past the age of seeing it as a guide or challenge to my own life. If there’s nothing in the book for you personally, it’s one you will likely still enjoy just to read about Amy’s experiences.<br />My thanks to NetGalley and Lake Union Publishing for providing me with an advanced read copy of this book in exchange for an unbiased review. It’s a book I highly recommend to anyone who enjoys a well-told tale and especially for anyone wanting to read about someone embarking on new experiences.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="18380091683067762720" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer12527289832070620268"><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>"And yes , it makes me crazy to think that my kids can go days— or maybe weeks—without me. If I’m not needed, if I’m not busy, if I’m not an overstretched, overwhelmed, underslept, underpaid single mother… What exactly am I?"</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br/><br/><b>📖The Overdue Life of Amy Byler📖</b><br/><b>🖋Kelly Harms </b><br/><br/><i>Much thanks to NetGalley, Lake Union Publishing and Kelly Harms for this complimentary copy. This review is voluntary and opinions are fully my own.</i><br/><br/><b>BUY THE BOOK : <a href='https://www.amazon.com/Overdue-Life-Amy-Byler-ebook/dp/B07GVK5HW8/ref=sr_1_3?crid=21KEB71RUA35G&keywords=kelly+harms&qid=1558690983&s=gateway&sprefix=kelly+harms%2Caps%2C573&sr=8-3' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>Amazon</a> * <a href='https://www.barnesandnoble.com/w/the-overdue-life-of-amy-byler-kelly-harms/1129597908#reviews-header' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>Barnes & Noble</a> * <a href='https://www.bookdepository.com/Overdue-Life-Amy-Byler-Kelly-Harms/9781542040570?ref=grid-view&qid=1558691107069&sr=1-1' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>Book Depository</a></b><br/><br/><br/><b>📚 Series: </b> No<br/><b>📚 </b></span>
  <span id="freeText12527289832070620268" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>"And yes , it makes me crazy to think that my kids can go days— or maybe weeks—without me. If I’m not needed, if I’m not busy, if I’m not an overstretched, overwhelmed, underslept, underpaid single mother… What exactly am I?"</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br /><br /><b>📖The Overdue Life of Amy Byler📖</b><br /><b>🖋Kelly Harms </b><br /><br /><i>Much thanks to NetGalley, Lake Union Publishing and Kelly Harms for this complimentary copy. This review is voluntary and opinions are fully my own.</i><br /><br /><b>BUY THE BOOK : <a href="https://www.amazon.com/Overdue-Life-Amy-Byler-ebook/dp/B07GVK5HW8/ref=sr_1_3?crid=21KEB71RUA35G&amp;keywords=kelly+harms&amp;qid=1558690983&amp;s=gateway&amp;sprefix=kelly+harms%2Caps%2C573&amp;sr=8-3" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Amazon</a> * <a href="https://www.barnesandnoble.com/w/the-overdue-life-of-amy-byler-kelly-harms/1129597908#reviews-header" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Barnes &amp; Noble</a> * <a href="https://www.bookdepository.com/Overdue-Life-Amy-Byler-Kelly-Harms/9781542040570?ref=grid-view&amp;qid=1558691107069&amp;sr=1-1" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Book Depository</a></b><br /><br /><br /><b>📚 Series: </b> No<br /><b>📚 Genre: </b> General Fiction / Romance<br /><b>📚 POV: </b> First person.<br /><b>📚 Cliffhanger: </b> No.<br /><br /><b>⚠ Content Warnings: </b> Cheating. Divorce. Accident/Surgery on a minor character.<br /><b>⚠ Read if: </b> you feel like you are underappreciated and need a break. Or, if you are looking for a light fun read.<br /><br />Amy Byler is an overworked and underpaid single mom of two children (Cori, 15 and Joe, 12) whose (common law ex-)husband went to Hong Kong and disappeared for three years.<br /><br />Out of nowhere, John (the ex husband) returns and wants to make amends with her and the kids. He offers to take care of them for the summer, and suddenly Amy is handed a whole lot of time in her hands.. and for the first time, nothing to do and no kids to think about.<br /><br />School librarian Amy suddenly decided to go to New York for a library conference. Reuniting with her college friend also led her to be part a "momspringa". At the prospect of being alone, Amy now has time to think her life over and make decisions on her marriage. If life suddenly gives her the opportunity for a whole lot of change in mindset and new love prospect, then, hey, let her take it.<br /><br /><i>
  <b>
    <blockquote>"Can forgiving him and enjoying time with him now actually make you feel better than holding a grudge against him for the rest of your lives? In other words, is punishing him what’s truly best for you?”</blockquote>
  </b>
</i><br /><br />Amy Byler is so likeable and relatable and made me appreciate my mom even more. I was rooting for her all the while and felt very happy with how life turned out for her.<br /><br />Her support system were lovable. We're here for girls supporting girls! The whole "momspringa" journey was so fun, it definitely felt like I was watching a movie!<br /><br />Her love interest is swoonworthy and perfectly written for her. I was nervous at first but now extremely happy with what happend in the end.<br /><br />I loved all the bits of literary references, too. The nerd in me was swimming in happiness!<br /><br />This book, in its entirety, is very charming and so funny you might laugh out loud, but also a very thought provoking and heart warming read.<br /><br /><b>☁ THE CRITERIA ☁</b><br /><b>🌻 Blurb:⭐⭐⭐⭐</b><br /><b>🌻 Hero:⭐⭐⭐⭐</b><br /><b>🌻 Heroine:⭐⭐⭐⭐⭐</b><br /><b>🌻 Support Characters:⭐⭐⭐⭐</b><br /><b>🌻 Writing Style:⭐⭐⭐⭐⭐</b><br /><b>🌻 Character Development:⭐⭐⭐⭐⭐</b><br /><b>🌻 Romance:⭐⭐⭐⭐</b><br /><b>🌻 Pacing:⭐⭐⭐⭐⭐</b><br /><b>🌻 Ending:⭐⭐⭐⭐⭐</b><br /><b>🌻 Page Turner:⭐⭐⭐⭐</b><br /><b>🌻 Book Cover:⭐⭐⭐⭐⭐</b><br /><br /><b> ☁FINAL VERDICT: </b> 4.63/5 ☁</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17418001846383713096">2 1/2 stars. This was my second book from Amazon Prime first reads, and it's probably a good indication that I should stick to well vetted and recommended reads. While the author touches on realistic issues (marriage problems, abandonment, struggles with the demands of motherhood), many of the proposed solutions to said issues (casual sex, drinking, getting makeovers, being "free") seem shallow and unlikely to actually fill the real needs of connection and purpose. Additionally, despite being "i</span>
  <span id="freeText17418001846383713096" style="display:none">2 1/2 stars. This was my second book from Amazon Prime first reads, and it's probably a good indication that I should stick to well vetted and recommended reads. While the author touches on realistic issues (marriage problems, abandonment, struggles with the demands of motherhood), many of the proposed solutions to said issues (casual sex, drinking, getting makeovers, being "free") seem shallow and unlikely to actually fill the real needs of connection and purpose. Additionally, despite being "in the trenches" of motherhood, the humor fell flat for me. I did enjoy the literary references.</span>
