              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15493045-lisa?shelf=kindle">kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15493045-lisa?shelf=2019">2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15493045-lisa?shelf=netgalley">netgalley</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15493045-lisa?shelf=netgalley2019">netgalley2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15493045-lisa?shelf=4-star-reviews">4-star-reviews</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2776616823" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11342781334239539993">Author Kelly Harms has started a thing with Amy Byler and her #momspringa and every mom is going to want one! Read about it here!<br/><br/>SUMMARY<br/>Amy Byler lives in a small town in Pennsylvania and is utterly shocked when she sees her missing husband, John, in her neighborhood drugstore. Three years ago, John went to Hong Kong and never came home. But, he is back now, and wants to spend a week with the children he abandoned: Cori, 15, and Joe, 11. He wants to fix things, make things right and be the fathe</span>
  <span id="freeText11342781334239539993" style="display:none">Author Kelly Harms has started a thing with Amy Byler and her #momspringa and every mom is going to want one! Read about it here!<br /><br />SUMMARY<br />Amy Byler lives in a small town in Pennsylvania and is utterly shocked when she sees her missing husband, John, in her neighborhood drugstore. Three years ago, John went to Hong Kong and never came home. But, he is back now, and wants to spend a week with the children he abandoned: Cori, 15, and Joe, 11. He wants to fix things, make things right and be the father he should have always been. <br /><br />After a tumultuous family meeting, the kids agree to hang with their dad for a week. Amy decides to take advantage of the week by attending a library educators’ conference and visiting a friend in NYC. She meets a "hot librarian" Daniel Seong-Eason, while at the conference and sparks fly. <br /><br />When John's week with Cori and Joe turns into a month, Amy stays in NYC, where she gets a new wardrobe and hairstyle and is featured in a fashion magazine managed by her college friend Talia, who also offers Amy her apartment, rent-free, for the summer. The magazine arranges a series of tantalizing dates for Amy’s “#momspringa” NYC adventure, which is trending on social media. Amy is soon torn between her glamorous life in New York and the needs of her children at home. <br /><br />REVIEW<br />This book is absolutely adorable. It’s light and laugh out loud funny and will capture your attention as well as your imagination. I couldn’t put it down. It’s easy and fun to read, and particularly would appeal to those hard-working mom’s that never seem to get a break. The Overdue Life of Amy Byler is clever and gives us all something to think about. <br /><br />I was drawn to Kelly Harms’ librarian humor and book references, especially the shout out to Ann Patchett, my favorite author; and salt and vinegar potato chips, my favorite snack. How did she know! Amy’s friends, Talia and Lena were the best, and I loved, loved, loved their text exchanges. Totally agree with Amy that every mom should have a #momspringa! Oh, and by the way...I’m attending a library conference in Florida in two weeks! Lol! <br /><br />Author Kelly Harms is an author, a mother and a big dreamer. She lives in Madison, Wisconsin, with her sparkling son, Griffin; her fluffy dog, Scout; and her beloved Irishman, Chris. Before this midwestern life, she lived in New York City and worked with many of her author-heroes as an editor at HarperCollins, and then as a literary agent. at the Jane Rotrosen Agency.<br /><br />Publisher 	Lake Union<br />Published 	May 1, 2019<br />Review	<a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.bluestockingreviews.com">www.bluestockingreviews.com</a><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="11342781334239539993" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2773827467" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2773827467" />
    <a title="abby" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44478099-abby"><img alt="abby" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597252036p2/44478099.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2773827467?book_show_action=true">Apr 04, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="abby" class="user" itemprop="url" name="abby" href="/user/show/44478099-abby">abby</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/42399951-the-overdue-life-of-amy-byler">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44478099-abby?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44478099-abby?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44478099-abby?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2773827467" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14144528380509624254">I needed something quick and fun to read, and this book fit the bill. It's pretty stereotypical chick-lit. The woman has been wronged by a man who comes back to make amends and gets a fun vacation to NY out of the deal where every guy is either her gay best friend or wants to sleep with her. Confused feelings about the men in her life, conflicted about what she wants out of life, cue in some deepish thoughts. Happy endings all around.<br/><br/>The one knock I have about this book is the way the teenage ch</span>
  <span id="freeText14144528380509624254" style="display:none">I needed something quick and fun to read, and this book fit the bill. It's pretty stereotypical chick-lit. The woman has been wronged by a man who comes back to make amends and gets a fun vacation to NY out of the deal where every guy is either her gay best friend or wants to sleep with her. Confused feelings about the men in her life, conflicted about what she wants out of life, cue in some deepish thoughts. Happy endings all around.<br /><br />The one knock I have about this book is the way the teenage character talk and interact with their parents. A 12 year old boy uses the word "darling" unironically for one example. An adult man introduces his girlfriend to his teen daughter by calling her "sexy." When I was fifteen, I would have vomited if my father had called my own mother sexy, much less some woman I've never met before but deep down know my father is sleeping with. Look, I know it's 2019 and every parents wants to be woke (after they Google what that's supposed to mean) and the cool mom or dad, but teens are still teens and they still hide periods from their dad and the fact that their new boyfriend felt them up from their moms. It just felt unnatural. A lot of the dialogue did.<br /><br />Ask me in a week what this book was about and I probably won't be able to remember. But I had fun reading it, and that's all I wanted.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14144528380509624254" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2798430202" />
    <a title="mindful.librarian ☀️" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13650342-mindful-librarian"><img alt="mindful.librarian ☀️" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1581440560p2/13650342.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2798430202?book_show_action=true">Apr 26, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="mindful.librarian ☀️" class="user" itemprop="url" name="mindful.librarian ☀️" href="/user/show/13650342-mindful-librarian">mindful.librarian ☀️</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9781542040570" href="/book/show/41723457-the-overdue-life-of-amy-byler">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13650342-mindful-librarian?shelf=advanced-reader-copies">advanced-reader-copies</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13650342-mindful-librarian?shelf=adult-reads">adult-reads</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2798430202" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13520523721823826512">(free review copy) As a school librarian and a 38-year-old mom of 3, I feel like I'm the EXACT target audience for this book! I related to so much of the story and I loved all the nerdy bookish references. So much fabulous humor in the journal entries and emails from Amy's teen daughters, as well as in her interactions with her 2 friends via text and in person. All around a perfect fun read for any mom you know! Great Mother's Day present.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Nkfvat1r3KA6zhUc41qVvvO9dpA3tbKrZlhtatPAlrfLkgODkN9y3UYpcRPhHOo1e/T+xe25MLtiDBZorBVVcA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('EFcDV9qPxneJfLUT4fTLR1WL/V3T3cc0eERzOSfQjtjtgu++lztoCvWb0RzjsrTM3cJ1CAnRRSR8EAg7WAVNHw==')})
  }

Like you’re at a party but all the good stuff is happening out of earshot (#FOMO)? That’s life—especially for an immigrant.What happens when a shy, awkward Arab girl with a weird name and an unfortunate propensity toward facial hair is uprooted from her comfortable (albeit fascist-regimed) homeland of Iraq and thrust into the cold, alien town of Columbus, Ohio—with its Egg McMuffins, Barbie dolls, and kids playing doctor everywhere you turned?This is Ayser Salman’s story. First comes Emigration, then Naturalization, and finally Assimilation—trying to fit in among her blonde-haired, blue-eyed counterparts, and always feeling left out. On her journey to Americanhood, Ayser sees more naked butts at pre-kindergarten daycare that she would like, breaks one of her parents’ rules (“Thou shalt not participate as an actor in the school musical where a male cast member rests his head in thy lap”), and other things good Muslim Arab girls are not supposed to do. And, after the 9/11 attacks, she experiences the isolation of being a Muslim in her own country. It takes hours of therapy, fifty-five rounds of electrolysis, and some ill-advised romantic dalliances for Ayser to grow into a modern Arab American woman who embraces her cultural differences.Part memoir and part how-not-to guide, The Wrong End of the Table is everything you wanted to know about Arabs but were afraid to ask, with chapters such as “Tattoos and Other National Security Risks,” “You Can’t Blame Everything on Your Period; Sometimes You’re Going to Be a Crazy Bitch: and Other Advice from Mom,” and even an open letter to Trump. This is the story of every American outsider on a path to find themselves in a country of beautiful diversity.<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"7856162028670628800\" href=\"#\" Despite their extraordinary bond, they eventually find themselves facing the ultimate crisis of their marriage—a deception that will lead to the unraveling of everything they’ve fought so hard for. <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer7377726205685959125">USA Today, Washington Post and Amazon Charts bestseller Kelly Harms is the author of The Bright Side of Going Dark, The Overdue Life of Amy Byler, The Good Luck Girls of Shipwreck Lane and The Matchmakers of Minnow Bay. She worked with bestselling authors, Edgar, RITA, and Agatha award winners, and Indie Next List Picks in her time as an editor at a division of HarperCollins and later as an agent </span>
  <span id="freeText7377726205685959125" style="display:none">USA Today, Washington Post and Amazon Charts bestseller Kelly Harms is the author of The Bright Side of Going Dark, The Overdue Life of Amy Byler, The Good Luck Girls of Shipwreck Lane and The Matchmakers of Minnow Bay. She worked with bestselling authors, Edgar, RITA, and Agatha award winners, and Indie Next List Picks in her time as an editor at a division of HarperCollins and later as an agent at the Jane Rotrosen Agency. She now lives in Madison, Wisconsin with her beloved family.<br /></span>
